## III Hyperkalaemia in Resuscitation (Guidelines 26.1 – 26.2)

##### Guideline 26.1 – Hyperkalaemia; Prevention of Cardiac Arrest in Hyperkalaemia

We recommend that hyperkalaemia is treated urgently in patients with severe hyperkalaemia (K⁺ ≥ 6.5 mmol/l) and in those with ECG changes suggestive of severe hyperkalaemia. (1C)

##### Guideline 26.2 – Hyperkalaemia; Prevention of Cardiac Arrest in Hyperkalaemia

We recommend continuous cardiac monitoring for patients with severe hyperkalaemia ( $ K^+ \geq 6.5 $ mmol/l) in a setting appropriate for the level of care required. (1C)

#### Rationale (Guidelines 26.1 – 26.2)

The outcome of hyperkalaemic cardiac arrest is generally poor, therefore efforts to avoid its occurrence in the first instance is the best approach.

Early recognition, a high index of suspicion in patients at risk and prompt intervention can reduce the risk of cardiac arrest in patients with hyperkalaemia. Initiation of treatment prior to confirmation of hyperkalaemia is warranted if the suspicion of hyperkalaemia is high. Look for toxic ECG changes which may precede cardiac arrest - wide QRS complex, bradycardia or sine wave (Guidelines 14.1-14.2; Figure 3). Limb weakness is an ominous sign. Cardiac monitoring is essential to detect arrhythmias.

The ECG is a helpful tool in risk stratification. Durfey et al found that adverse events including symptomatic bradycardia (n=22), VT (n=2), CPR (n=2) and death (n=4) occurred prior to administration of IV calcium and all but one event occurred before administration of K⁺-lowering medication.¹ This highlights the importance of timely treatment to prevent arrhythmias and cardiac arrest.

Treat severe hyperkalaemia as a medical emergency.

IV calcium is a crucial step in the prevention of arrhythmias and cardiac arrest in hyperkalaemia. $ ^{2} $ Ensure that the appropriate dose is administered (30ml Calcium Gluconate over 10 minutes IV) to stabilise the heart. Adverse events have been noted when an inappropriate dose of IV calcium is administered. $ ^{3} $ Vigilance is also required as toxic ECG changes may recur when the effect of IV calcium has worn off after approximately 30-60 minutes.

Unfortunately, delays in treatment are well recognised and has resulted in patient harm. $ ^{4,5} $ The potential for clinical deterioration may not be appreciated by medical or nursing staff prior to cardiac arrest. Refer early for specialist advice particularly for patients with ESRD and those who do not respond to medical treatment. Blood monitoring is essential to assess efficacy of treatment and for re-bound hyperkalaemia. Rebound may also occur after dialysis and may be exaggerated if temporising drugs have been used. $ ^{6} $

There are a few fallacies related to hyperkalaemia that require clarification:

Patients with pacemakers are not protected from hyperkalaemic cardiac arrest. Indeed, pacemaker failure has been well documented in this circumstance. $ ^{7,8} $

The presence of a normal ECG in the context of severe hyperkalaemia is not protective against arrhythmias.

■ Severe hyperkalaemia can occur in the presence of near normal renal function, but may be assumed to be spurious. An urgent ECG and repeat blood sample using a blood gas analyser should confirm the presence of hyperkalaemia.

Patients receiving longterm haemodialysis do not have a ‘tolerance’ to severe hyperkalaemia and are also at risk of cardiac arrest. Medical treatment will only temporarily lower the serum  $ K^{+} $, therefore urgent dialysis is indicated.

## III Hyperkalaemia in Resuscitation (Guidelines 27.1)

##### Guideline 27.1 – Hyperkalaemia; Algorithm in Cardiac Arrest

We recommend that cardiac arrest attributable to hyperkalaemia is managed using the treatment algorithm which provides guidance on the medical therapies and the need for initiation of renal replacement therapy during CPR. (1C)

#### Rationale (Guidelines 27.1)

Hyperkalaemia is a potentially reversible cause of cardiac arrest, but achieving and sustaining ROSC is dependent on controlling the serum K⁺ level. In this way, this special circumstance is analogous to hypothermic cardiac arrest. There are fewer drug therapy options for controlling hyperkalaemia during cardiac arrest (Guidelines 25.1 - 25.3) and the degree of K⁺-lowering required to achieve ROSC may not be achievable with drugs alone (Guideline 25.4). The hyperkalaemic cardiac arrest algorithm outlines the modifications to ALS and the specific interventions to address hyperkalaemia as illustrated in Appendix 8.

word-wrap: break-word;'>Entraps  $ K^{+} $ in exchange for  $ Ca^{2+} $</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Non-specific binding of  $ K^{+} $ in exchange for  $ Ca^{2+} $</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Selective  $ K^{+} $ binding in exchange for  $ Na^{+} $</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Site of action</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Distal Colon</td><td style='text-align: center; ### Appendix 4A: Drug administration and safety - IV CALCIUM PREPARATIONS


<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td colspan="2">Calcium Chloride</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Available as</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Calcium chloride 10% pre-filled syringe 10mL (contains 6.8mmol of calcium in 10mL) $ ^{[1]} $</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Preparation</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Can be used undiluted</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Flush solutions</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Flush well with sodium chloride 0.9% to reduce vein irritation. · Incompatible with many solutions (including sodium bicarbonate and phosphate).</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Administration</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Give by intravenous injection over 5 minutes in peri-arrest setting. $ ^{[1,2]} $ · Give as a bolus injection during cardiopulmonary resuscitation. · Preferably administer via a central venous device (if already in-situ). · For peripheral administration, choose a large vein and monitor closely for phlebitis. · Ensure patient is supine and closely observed during injection. · Monitor ECG and blood pressure.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Specialist technical information</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Extravasation can cause tissue damage because of the high osmolarity.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Cautions and side effects</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Cautions: - Hypercalcaemia. Digoxin. · Side Effects: - Too rapid administration may lead to symptoms of hypercalcaemia and may cause cardiac arrhythmias or arrest, hypotension and vasomotor collapse, sweating, hot flushes, nausea and vomiting.</td></tr></table>


<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td colspan="2">Calcium Gluconate</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Available as</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Calcium gluconate 10% ampoules (contains 2.2mmol of calcium in 10mL) $ ^{[3,4]} $</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Preparation</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Can be used undiluted.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Flush solutions</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Flush well with sodium chloride 0.9% or glucose 5% to avoid vein irritation. · Incompatible with many solutions (including sodium bicarbonate and phosphate).</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Administration</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Give 30ml 10% Calcium Gluconate IV over 10 minutes. $ ^{[2-6]} $ · For peripheral administration, choose a large vein and monitor closely for phlebitis. · Ensure patient is supine and closely observed during injection. · Monitoring ECG and blood pressure.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Specialist technical information</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Extravasation can cause tissue damage because of the high osmolarity.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Cautions and side effects</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Cautions: - Hypercalcaemia. Digoxin. · Side-Effects: - Administer slowly to minimise peripheral vasodilation, cardiac depression and circulatory collapse.</td></tr></table>

Appendix 4B: Drug administration and safety – INSULIN-GLUCOSE INFUSION


<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td colspan="2">10 units of Soluble Insulin in 50mL Glucose 50% (25g)</td></tr><tr><td rowspan="2">Available as</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Vials containing human soluble insulin 100 units per mL (Actrapid $ ^{\circledR} $)</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Vials containing 50mL glucose 50% (25g)</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Preparation</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>• Withdraw 10 units of Actrapid $ ^{\circledR} $ insulin. This should be done only using an insulin syringe which is graduated in units. Due to the potential for dosing errors, it is recommended that this is independently checked by another healthcare professional. • Inject the insulin into a 50mL glucose 50% vial and mix well. • Withdraw contents of vial into 50mL intravenous syringe.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Final concentration</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>10 units soluble insulin in 50mL</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Dilution/flush solutions</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Sodium chloride 0.9% - flush well to reduce vein irritation</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Administration</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>IV Injection: Administered over 5-15 minutes intravenously into a large vein Monitor for phlebitis if 50% glucose is given peripherally.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Storage and handling</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Do not use unless solution is clear and without visible particles.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Specialist technical information</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Glucose 50% has a high osmolarity and administration into a peripheral vein may result in vein irritation, vein damage and thrombosis.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Cautions and side effects</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>• Hypoglycaemia - follow monitoring recommendations in guideline and treat according to local guidelines. • Infusion site reactions including phlebitis, erythema and thrombophlebitis. • Hypersensitivity/ anaphylactic reactions have been reported thought to be due to corn allergy. Should be used with caution, if at all in patients with a known allergy to corn products.</td></tr></table>

### Appendix 4D: Drug administration and safety – PATIROMER


<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td colspan="2">Patiromer</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Available as</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>8.4g, 16.8g and 25.2g sachets</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Preparation</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>• The dose should be poured into a glass containing approximately 40mL of water and then stirred. • Another approximately 40mL of water should be added, and the suspension stirred again thoroughly. The powder will not dissolve. • More water may be added to the mixture as needed.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Administration</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>• Apple juice or cranberry juice can be used instead of water to prepare the mixture (be aware of potential interactions with cranberry juice). Other liquids should be avoided due to potential potassium content. • Can be taken with food or without food. • Administration should be separated by 3 hours from other medicines.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Storage and handling</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>• The reconstituted mixture should be taken within 1 hour of initial suspension. • Unopened storage and transportation should be refrigerated (2°C-8°C). Patients may store below 25°C for up to 6 months.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Cautions and side effects</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>• Cautions - Hypercalcaemia, hypomagnesaemia, GI disorders, contains sorbitol. • Side-effects -Hypomagnesaemia, constipation, diarrhoea, abdominal pain and flatulence</td></tr></table>

## References

1. Electronic Medicines Compendium: Summary of Product Characteristics – Veltassa (Patiromer).

Vifor Fresenius Medical Care Renal Pharma UK Ltd. Available at https://www.medicines.org.uk/emc/product/779. Last updated 21 July 2021.

<div style="text-align: center;">Appendix 4E: Drug administration and safety – SODIUM ZIRCONIUM CYCLOSILICATE</div>



<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td colspan="2">Sodium Zirconium Cyclosilicate</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Available as</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>5g, 10g sachets (powder oral suspension)</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Preparation</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· The contents of the sachet should be emptied into a glass containing approximately 45mL of water and stirred well. The powder will not dissolve. · Advise patient to drink the tasteless liquid while still cloudy. · If the suspension settles - it should be stirred again.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Administration</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· The suspension can be taken with or without food. · Administer at least 2 hours before or 2 hours after oral medications with clinically meaningful gastric pH dependent bioavailability.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Treatment: Correction Phase</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· SZC 10g three times daily until normokalaemia (serum  $ K^{+} $ 4.0 - 5.0 mmol/l) achieved. · Usually duration is 24 - 48 hours, maximum duration 72 hours. · Discontinue after 72 hours if normokalaemia not achieved.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Treatment: Maintenance Phase</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· SZC 5g daily starting dose (after normokalaemia achieved) · Titrate up to 10g once daily or down to 5g alternate days guided by serum  $ K^{+} $ levels. · Monitor serum  $ K^{+} $ level regularly. · Discontinue of hypokalaemia develops (serum  $ K^{+} $ &lt; 4.0 mmol/l)</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Cautions and side effects</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Cautions - can cause QT interval lengthening as a result of a reduction in serum potassium. May be opaque to X-rays - consider if having abdominal X-rays. · Side effects - Hypokalaemia, oedema, gastrointestinal disorders.</td></tr></table>

## References

1. Electronic Medicines Compendium: Summary of Product Characteristics – Lokelma 10g powder for oral suspension. AstraZeneca UK Limited. Available at https://www.medicines.org.uk/emc/product/10074/smpc. Last updated 18 May 2023.

### Appendix 4F: Drug administration and safety – CALCIUM RESONIUM


<table border=1 style='margin: auto; word-wrap: break-word;'><tr><td colspan="2">Calcium Resonium</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Available as</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Calcium Resonium Powder (99.934%)</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Preparation</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Oral administration:-  ○ Each 1g of resin should be mixed with 3 to 4mL of  water or syrup (not fruit juices). This corresponds  to 45 to 60mL of liquid for a 15g dose.  · Rectal administration  ○ 30g of resin should be mixed with 150mL of water  or glucose 10% as a daily retention enema.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Administration</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· For oral administration, administer at least 3 hours before,  or 3 hours after other medication. In patients with  gastroparesis consider a 6-hour separation.  · For rectal administration, the enema should be retained for  at least 9 hours then the colon should be irrigated to  remove the resin.</td></tr><tr><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>Cautions and side effects</td><td style='text-align: center; word-wrap: break-word;'>· Contra-indicated in hypercalcaemia or in obstructive bowel disease.  · Concomitant use with sorbitol is not recommended due to  gastro-intestinal stenosis and intestinal ischaemia.</td></tr></table>

## References

1. Electronic Medicines Compendium: Summary of Product Characteristics – Calcium Resonium 99.934% w/w powder for oral/rectal suspension. Sanofi. Available at https://www.medicines.org.uk/emc/product/1439. Last updated 8 August 2022.
